## Ezra 9:5–15 (id: eng-ezr-p19b-v1)

Hear and Heart
--------------

In this step, hear Ezra 9:5–15 and put it in your hearts.

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 9:5–15 three times, in three different translations, if possible.

Pause this audio here.

Now, as a group, discuss the following questions:

1. What do you like in this passage? Pause this audio here.
2. What do you not like or not understand in this passage? Pause this audio here.
3. What does this passage tell us about God? Pause this audio here.
4. What does this passage tell us about people? Pause this audio here.
5. How does this passage affect our daily lives? Pause this audio here.
6. Who do you know who needs to hear this passage?

Setting the Stage
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 9:5–15 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

This passage directly follows the previous passage. You will remember that the leaders of the Israelites in Jerusalem told Ezra that the Israelites in Jerusalem married people who were not Israelites and who did not obey Yahweh. Ezra was horrified and sat down to mourn for the Israelite people. Ezra sat and mourned until the evening. Some Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh came to be with Ezra. We do not know how many Israelites are with Ezra, or if they are only men or men and women. The previous story and this story take place in front of the temple in Jerusalem.

At the end of the day, at the time when the priests perform the evening offering, Ezra moves and gets up from his sitting position. Ezra's tunic and cloak are torn.

Stop here and, as a group, look at a picture of a person wearing a tunic. Pause this audio here.

Stop here and, as a group, look at a picture of a person wearing a cloak. Pause this audio here.

Ezra does not change his clothes. Ezra falls to his knees to show Yahweh that Ezra is humble. Ezra is not proud and does not feel good enough to stand in front of Yahweh. Ezra does not fall from a height or because he loses his balance. Ezra moves onto his knees quickly. It was more common for Israelites to pray to Yahweh standing or sitting. Ezra prays to Yahweh while on his knees to show that Ezra does not deserve respect. Ezra spreads out his hands to show that Ezra needs Yahweh's help.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How do you pray to God? How does a person's position of their body change if the person is praising God, saying sorry to God, or asking for help? Pause this audio here.

Then, Ezra prays to Yahweh. Ezra prays out loud. Sometimes, Ezra talks to Yahweh personally, and at other times, Ezra uses his words in the prayer to talk to the people around him as well as to Yahweh. Ezra feels ashamed and embarrassed.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Have one person pretend to have done something terrible and need to tell another person in the group what they have done wrong. Help the person who is pretending to have done something terrible to use their body to show how bad they feel. Pause this audio here.

Ezra calls on God, the almighty Creator God. Ezra does not use "Yahweh," God's personal name. Ezra addresses God directly as the God whom Ezra worships. Ezra bows his head to show how he feels. At Ezra's time, people looked up to imagine God in front of or above them. This was a usual way for people to worship and pray to God. Ezra did not feel able to look up to pray to Yahweh. Ezra uses creative language to talk about how big and how serious the Israelites' sins are. Ezra includes himself among the people who have sinned. Ezra talks about all the Israelites' guilt because the Israelites had disobeyed Yahweh for a long time.

Ezra knows all the bad things that happened to the Israelites because of the sins of the Israelite people. You may remember from the books of 2 Kings and 2 Chronicles that the Assyrians and Babylonians killed many Israelites and took many Israelites from Jerusalem to Babylon. The Babylonians stole the Israelites' belongings. The Babylonian and Assyrian kings shamed the Israelites. At the time of Ezra, the king of Persia reigned over the Israelites and the land Yahweh gave to the Israelites. You may remember that the Persians took control of Babylon and everything that the Babylonians owned.

Stop here and talk about a time when another people group ruled or controlled your land and people. What did the other people do to your people to show that they were in control of your people and your land? Pause this audio here.

Ezra continues to pray to God, and Ezra uses God's personal name, Yahweh. Ezra prays for everyone, and Ezra includes himself. Ezra talks about a short amount of time. This is about 80 years from the first return of the exiles to the present time for Ezra. Ezra knows that Yahweh was kind, generous, and showed mercy to the Israelites. Yahweh allowed a remnant, a small part of something, to remain. This remnant is the Israelites who survived the exile and came back to Jerusalem with Zerubbabel and Ezra. Yahweh gave the Israelites a small but secure hold in Yahweh's holy place, the rebuilt temple or Jerusalem.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Talk about how your people arrived at the land where they now live. Pay particular attention to any part of the story that relates to how people claimed or took hold of the land. Pause this audio here.

Ezra says God gave light to Ezra and the Israelites' eyes. Yahweh gave hope and revived Ezra and the Israelites. God gave Ezra and the Israelites a better life in Jerusalem compared to life in Babylon. The Israelites are still slaves to the Persians, and there are still some Israelites in Babylon. The Persians own the Israelites, and the Israelites have to work for the Persians. However, God has not left or abandoned the Israelites as slaves in Babylon. God has shown kindness to the Israelites. We do not know if Ezra thinks the kings of Persia see God's love for the Israelites or if Ezra thinks God prompted the kings of Persia to make life better for the Israelites. Either way, God has caused the kings of Persia to make life better for the Israelites. During the brief time since Yahweh rescued the Israelites from exile in Babylon, Yahweh gave the Israelites permission to rebuild and repair the temple in Jerusalem. This happened before Ezra's time, but Ezra thanks God here. When the Persians allowed the Israelites to rebuild their temple, it was like the Israelites had a new and wonderful life! Ezra also says that Yahweh has given the Israelites a wall of protection in Judah and Jerusalem. Ezra does not mean an actual wall that people make from stone or bricks. Ezra means that the Persians are like a wall that gives protection to people and keeps the people safe. God is protecting the Israelites by causing the Persians to protect and keep the people safe.

Now Ezra asks God a question that he does not expect God to answer. Ezra uses the question to ask what the Israelites can do after everything that Ezra spoke about in the first part of Ezra's prayer. Ezra knows that the Israelites cannot do anything because the Israelites have disobeyed Yahweh's laws. Yahweh gave the laws or commands to Moses and other prophets who served Yahweh. Ezra remembers the laws in his prayer. First, Ezra quotes the law Yahweh gave to Moses that Moses wrote in Deuteronomy.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: If possible, listen to your translation of Deuteronomy 7:1–3 in your own language as a group. Pause this audio here.

You will remember that Yahweh spoke to Moses about the Israelites going into and taking the promised land, Canaan. Yahweh describes the land as unclean because the Canaanite people make the land unclean with their abominations or detestable practices. The Canaanite people worship false gods. Yahweh commanded the Israelites not to marry the people who lived in Canaan. Yahweh also told Moses that the Israelites must not live peacefully with or be friends with the Canaanites. Yahweh did not want the Israelites to make a treaty of friendship with the people in Canaan. A treaty is an official agreement between two groups of people.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Talk about a time when two groups of people met each other and made friends with each other. Pause this audio here.

Ezra quotes three blessings Moses wrote in Deuteronomy about how Yahweh will bless the Israelites if the Israelites follow Yahweh's commands. Yahweh will make the nation of Israel strong. Yahweh will give good things from the land to the Israelites. Yahweh will make it possible for the Israelites to pass the land from one generation to the next as an inheritance.

Ezra now starts the last part of his prayer to Yahweh. Ezra says to God and the people listening to Ezra that the deaths and exile of the Israelites happened because the Israelites disobeyed Yahweh. Ezra prays for himself and the Israelites but does not use "Yahweh," the personal name for God. Ezra thanks God for showing mercy and not punishing the Israelites with death. In Ezra's prayer, Ezra asks God and the Israelites a question that he does not expect God or the people to answer. Ezra asks if the Israelites should break Yahweh's laws again and marry people who are not Israelites. Ezra hopes that the Israelites will repent of the sin they did. Ezra wants the people who are listening to Ezra to answer "No" to Ezra's question.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Talk about people in your community who have married people from outside of your community. Pause this audio here.

Ezra then asks God and the Israelites another question that Ezra does not expect God or the people to answer. Ezra asks if God would be angry enough to destroy the Israelites if the Israelites marry people who are not Israelites. Ezra knows that Yahweh's anger at sin can kill all the Israelites. Ezra wants the people who are listening to Ezra to answer "Yes" to Ezra's question.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Pretend to be parents trying to teach a child to do the right thing. What questions can a "parent" use to help teach the child? Try to ask questions of a child that the parent does not expect the child to answer. Pause this audio here.

Ezra directly talks to Yahweh, the God of Israel, to declare the truth that Yahweh is righteous. Ezra again states the fact that Yahweh has been good to leave a remnant, or small part of Israel, alive. Ezra has hope because Yahweh left a remnant before when the Israelites were disobedient. Ezra talks about the Israelites at Ezra's time. Ezra knows that Yahweh sees the Israelites as disobedient people who know that they have disobeyed Yahweh. In Ezra's time, someone who was not guilty of a crime stood before the judge so the judge could allow the person to go free. The Israelites cannot stand before God because the Israelites know they are guilty.

Defining the Scenes
-------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 9:5–15 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will define the scenes, characters, and setting of this passage. Then the group will visualize this passage.

This passage has five scenes.

**In the first scene:** Ezra stands up. Then Ezra kneels and spreads out his hands and starts to pray.

**In the second scene:** Ezra continues to pray to his God. Ezra says he is ashamed. The Israelites are guilty of lots of sins. Foreign kings captured and killed the Israelites because of the Israelites' sins.

**In the third scene:** In the next part of Ezra's prayer, Ezra prays to Yahweh, the God of Ezra and the Israelites. Ezra thanks Yahweh for showing the Israelites grace and mercy and for bringing some Israelites back to Jerusalem.

**In the fourth scene:** Ezra continues to pray to his and the Israelites' God. Ezra confesses that the Israelites have disobeyed God. Ezra quotes Yahweh's commands to Moses and the blessings for obedient Israelites.

**In the fifth scene:** Ezra finishes his prayer to God. Ezra thanks God for God's mercy to the Israelites. Ezra asks why the Israelites should test God again. Ezra tells Yahweh that Yahweh can judge Ezra and the Israelites.

The characters in this passage are:

* Ezra
* Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh's commands
* Israelites who were unfaithful to Yahweh's commands
* And Yahweh

As a group, pay attention to these parts of the passage's setting:

This passage happens on the same day as the previous passage. We do not know how long Ezra sat with torn clothes. This passage starts in the evening of that day, when it was time for the evening offering. The priests make the evening offering at the end of the day when the sun is very low in the sky, close to sunset. Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh's commands are with Ezra. We do not know how many Israelites are with Ezra, or if these people are only men or men and women.

Ezra moves from sitting to standing and then to being on his knees. When Ezra moves to being on his knees, Ezra spreads out his hands in front of him. Ezra's arms and hands are probably in the air, not on the ground. Ezra bows his head down with his face toward the ground.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: If possible, sit on the ground. Then, move from sitting to standing and then move quickly onto your knees. Use your body's weight to drop down onto your knees. Reach out in front of you with your arms and hands. Now describe to each other the movements you made. Pause this audio here.

Ezra starts to pray. Ezra uses the prayer to speak to the people around Ezra as well as to pray to God. Ezra prays out loud. Ezra talks to God about how he feels. Ezra feels ashamed and embarrassed. When a person is embarrassed, a person may blush or have a red face. Ezra uses creative language to describe in a visual way something that people cannot see. Ezra says that his and the Israelites' iniquities, or sins, are higher than their heads. Ezra says that the Israelites' sins are so many that if someone were to put the sins in a pile, the pile would be taller than the people. Then Ezra says that his and the Israelites' guilt has reached to the heavens, all the way to Yahweh. In other words, the Israelites no longer have a right relationship with God because the Israelites have sinned. At the time of Ezra, it was common to think of Yahweh as being high up in the heavens away from the earth. Ezra says the Israelites' sin and guilt are very, very big. The guilt reaching the heavens is a way for Ezra to emphasize the huge amount of sins and for Ezra to say it in a strong way.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What creative or special language do you use to describe something very big in size or number? Pause this audio here.

Ezra talks about a time long ago by calling it the days of the Israelites' ancestors or fathers. Ezra means the people who were alive a long time ago. Ezra talks about a period of time from when the Babylonians captured the Israelites until Ezra's present time. Ezra talks to his God about the bad things that happened to the Israelites during their time in exile and says that the same things are happening to Ezra's people on the day of Ezra's prayer. Ezra also says that God gives the people into the hands, or power, of the kings of the lands nearby. Ezra talks about people using the sword against the Israelites to represent Babylonians, Assyrians, and Persians killing Israelites.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What words or phrases do you use to talk indirectly about people killing other people? Pause this audio here.

Ezra stops praying about past events and starts to pray about the Israelites at Ezra's present time. In this part of the prayer, Ezra speaks to the Israelite people around him as well as to God. Ezra does not talk directly to God but refers to God like a person in a story. Ezra calls God by the personal name of Yahweh. Ezra knows that Yahweh has shown favor, or grace and mercy, to the Israelites by giving the Israelites good things. Ezra includes himself in the Israelite people. Ezra describes the Israelites who are still alive as a remnant, a surviving portion of the Israelites.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How would you describe a small group of people who were part of a larger group of people? Pause this audio here.

Ezra says that Yahweh has given the Israelites a secure hold or a firm place in Yahweh's holy place. In the original language, the Israelites used the word for a secure hold to refer to a place the people reach after a long journey. It can also mean a claim to a plot of land. Ezra uses special language to describe how God gives hope and encouragement to the Israelites. God used the good things to brighten or give light to the Israelite's eyes.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What imaginative ways do you use to talk about a person helping another person to have hope or to encourage another person? Pause this audio here.

Ezra talks about the ways God blesses the Israelites who are still alive at the time of Ezra. Ezra recognizes that the Israelites are still slaves. Ezra talks about God giving the Israelites a wall of protection. Ezra is using special language to talk about the Persian officials and government protecting the Israelites in Jerusalem and Judah. God is protecting the Israelites by causing the Persians to protect and keep the people safe.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What special language do you use to talk about something or someone giving protection to a person or people? Pause this audio here.

At this time in Ezra's prayer, Ezra talks directly to God again, but also speaks to the people around Ezra. Ezra prays to "our God" to speak for himself and the people around Ezra. Ezra does not use the personal name for God. Ezra uses a question that he does not expect anyone to answer to question what the Israelite people can say or do at the time of Ezra's prayer. Ezra says he and the Israelites are responsible for abandoning or not obeying God's laws. Ezra quotes from the law Yahweh gave to Moses before the Israelites entered Canaan. You may remember that the land of Canaan is unclean because the people who live there are unclean. This means that the people do detestable things, and that makes the people ritually unclean, or unfit to worship Yahweh. This is why Yahweh does not want the Israelites to do anything with these people or give their sons or daughters to marry these people. Yahweh did not want the Israelites to make a treaty or agreement to be friends with the other groups of people in Canaan.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Think about the activity in step two when you talked about two groups of people who agreed to be friends. What words did you use to describe the relationship between the two groups of people? Pause this audio here.

Then Ezra quotes the blessings Yahweh promised to the Israelites through Moses if the Israelites obeyed the law. If the Israelites avoid being friends with the people who live in the land of Canaan, the Israelites will be strong, and the land will be like an inheritance for their children.

Ezra finishes his prayer by speaking for the Israelites to God and to the Israelites around Ezra. Ezra uses his prayer to ask questions that he does not expect anyone to answer. Ezra asks what the Israelites will do next and what God will do to the Israelites. First, Ezra asks if the Israelites should break Yahweh's law on marriage again and intermarry with the people in the surrounding lands. Intermarriage describes when people from different social, racial, or religious groups marry each other. Ezra expects the answer to be no. Then, Ezra asks if their God's anger would be enough to destroy the rest of the Israelites if the Israelites continue to be unfaithful. At the end of Ezra's prayer, Ezra says what is true. Ezra calls on Yahweh, using the personal name for the God of Israel. Yahweh is just and righteous. The Israelites are a small surviving piece of the past larger nation, and the Israelites are guilty of disobeying Yahweh.

Now, the group should storyboard, draw, or use objects to visualize the passage and the action in it.

Embodying the Text
------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 9:5–15 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will dramatize the passage.

This passage has five scenes.

The characters in this passage are:

* Ezra
* Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh's commands
* Israelites who were unfaithful to Yahweh's commands
* And Yahweh

As a group, act out the passage twice. You should act out the passage in your own language.

First, act out the passage without stopping. Pay attention to the dialogue, flow, plotline, and chronology of the passage. Make sure you do not skip acting out the difficult or important parts of the passage. Help each other remember every part of the passage.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage.

The group should act out this passage a second time. At certain points in the drama, pause the drama and ask the person playing the character, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person playing the character should answer what they would be feeling or thinking if they were that character. Then continue the drama.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage a second time.

The following is an example of the drama and possible responses.

Ezra stands up. Then Ezra kneels and spreads out his hands and starts to pray.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I feel horrified and very sad; or
* What can we say to Yahweh? We do not deserve to live; or
* Maybe Yahweh will have mercy on us one more time?

Ask the person playing Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Look, Ezra is moving. What is Ezra going to do? or
* Should we pray too? or
* We feel very worried. We know some Israelites have disobeyed our God.

Continue the drama.

Ezra continues to pray to his God. Ezra says he is ashamed. The Israelites are guilty of lots of sins. Foreign kings captured and killed the Israelites because of the Israelites' sins.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I feel ashamed and embarrassed; or
* We have disobeyed God many, many times; or
* We are responsible for everything we have done wrong; or
* Our sins and disobedience caused our captivity and the death of our people.

Ask the person playing Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We feel guilty and ashamed; or
* Ezra is right. We are responsible for losing our land and becoming slaves.

Ask the person playing Israelites who were unfaithful to Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We were unfaithful and have not followed Yahweh's laws for us; or
* People captured and killed us because we did not keep Yahweh's laws.

Ask the person playing Yahweh, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I am glad Ezra is talking to me; or
* Ezra is right. My people have sinned many times and are guilty of disobeying me; or
* I am sad and disappointed. My Israelites did not stay separate from other people, and my Israelites disobeyed me.

Continue the drama.

In the next part of Ezra's prayer, Ezra prays to Yahweh, the God of Ezra and the Israelites. Ezra thanks Yahweh for showing the Israelites grace and mercy and bringing some Israelites back to Jerusalem.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Yahweh, thank you for giving us hope and helping us; or
* Yahweh still cares about us; or
* Yahweh has brought some of us home.

Ask the person playing Yahweh, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I love my people; or
* I have helped my people come home to Judah and Jerusalem; or
* The kings of Persia serve me to help my people.

Ask the person playing Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We are grateful. Yahweh brought us home to Jerusalem; or
* Life is better here; or
* We are happy because we have built the temple again and can live in Jerusalem.

Ask the person playing Israelites who were unfaithful to Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* It is good to live in Jerusalem; or
* We did not understand what God had done for us to keep us safe.

Continue the drama.

Ezra continues to pray to his and the Israelites' God. Ezra confesses that the Israelites have disobeyed God. Ezra quotes Yahweh's commands to Moses and the blessings for obedient Israelites.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I remember the law, and I love the law; or
* We have disobeyed Yahweh's commands to us; or
* Yahweh wants to bless us with good things for us and our children.

Ask the person playing Yahweh, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* You have broken my commands that I gave to Moses; or
* I want to bless my people if they obey me; or
* My people must not mix with people who do not worship me; or
* There is nothing you can do to make things right, but I will show mercy to you because I love my people.

Ask the person playing Israelites who were unfaithful to Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We forgot the laws; or
* We did not understand what we had to do to be Yahweh's people.

Ask the person playing Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* What can we do? Can we make sacrifices to Yahweh to say we are sorry? or
* We disobeyed God's law; or
* Yahweh could not bless us.

Continue the drama.

Ezra finishes his prayer to God. Ezra thanks God for God's mercy to the Israelites. Ezra asks why the Israelites should test God again. Ezra gives himself and the Israelites to Yahweh's judgement.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Yahweh has shown us mercy; or
* Will my people see and understand that they must change and not marry people from other lands? or
* I give myself and my people to Yahweh. I trust Yahweh to judge us.

Ask the person playing Yahweh, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I did show mercy to my people; or
* My people need to learn to obey my commands; or
* My people disobeyed me again. I will decide what happens to my people.

Ask the person playing Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Yahweh saved us even though we did not deserve Yahweh to save us; or
* We are angry. Some of our people have put us all in danger because they did not follow Yahweh's laws; or
* What will happen now? Will Yahweh save us again?

Ask the person playing Israelites who were unfaithful to Yahweh's commands, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* No, we will not break Yahweh's commands again; or
* We are frightened. Will Yahweh judge us guilty? or
* We are confused. Have we made a terrible mistake when we married women who lived here?

Filling the Gaps
----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 9:5–15 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will discuss key terms and words in this passage.

At the time of the evening offering, Ezra got up. Use the same word or phrase for **evening offering** or sacrifice as you used in previous passages. Refer to "offering" in the Master Glossary for more information.

Ezra got up from his time of humiliation when he mourned and tore his clothes. Ezra mourned, fasted, and made himself humble before Yahweh.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **humiliation**, the time when Ezra mourned for the people of Israel. Pause this audio here.

Ezra's **tunic** and **cloak** were torn. Use the same words or phrases for tunic and cloak as you used in previous passages. For more information on tunic and cloak, refer to the Master Glossary.

Ezra spread out his hands to **Yahweh**, Ezra's **God**. Yahweh is the personal name for God. Ezra's God created the whole world and is the God that the Israelites worship. Use the same words or phrases for Yahweh and God as you used in previous passages. For more information, look up Yahweh and God in the Master Glossary.

Ezra tells God that Ezra feels ashamed. Ezra feels embarrassed and guilty on behalf of his people.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **ashamed**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Ezra feels disgraced or embarrassed. Ezra feels like he has lost approval and respect from God.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **disgraced**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

The Israelites have many iniquities or sins. Iniquity is like sin, but it is a persistent and repeated behaviour that disobeys God.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **iniquity**. Look up iniquity in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

The Israelites' guilt has reached the heavens. Guilt is what a person has after they have sinned.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **guilt**. Look up guilt in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

The Israelites' guilt has reached the **heavens**. Ezra imagines the guilt reaching to the place where God lives with his angels. Use the same word or phrase for heaven as you used in previous passages. For more information, look up heaven in the Master Glossary.

Foreign **kings** killed and captured Israelite kings. A king is someone who rules over a city or a group of people. Look up king in the Master Glossary for more information and translate king in the same way you have previously.

Foreign kings killed and captured Israelite **priests**. Priests were people who worked in the temple of God in Jerusalem. Use the same word or phrase for priest as you used in previous passages. For more information, look up priest in the Master Glossary.

Yahweh, the Israelites' God, has shown the Israelites grace, or favor, that they did not deserve. God shows grace when he does good things for people that those people do not deserve. In this case, God has been kind to the Israelites by leaving a small group, or "remnant" of people, who are faithful to God.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **grace**. If you have already translated this idea in another part of the Bible, translate it here in a similar way. Pause this audio here.

Yahweh left a remnant of the Israelites. A remnant is a group of survivors who escape after enemies destroyed the rest of the people.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **remnant**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Yahweh gave the Israelites a place in Yahweh's holy place or sanctuary. A holy place is a place that people dedicate to God. Ezra means that the temple and also Jerusalem as a whole are Yahweh's holy place.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **holy place**. Look up **sanctuary** in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Yahweh has helped the Israelites in their **slavery**, or the life the Israelites live as slaves. Use the same word or phrase for slave as you used in previous passages, and refer to the Master Glossary for more information about slaves.

God has shown his steadfast love to the Israelites. Steadfast love is the loyal love of Yahweh, which does not change, become less, or end.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **steadfast love**. Look up steadfast love in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Ezra says that Yahweh allowed the Israelites to rebuild the "**house of our God**," the temple in Jerusalem. Look up "house of God" and temple in the Master Glossary for more information, but remember that Ezra specifies that it is the house of "our" God.

Yahweh has given the Israelites a wall of protection in **Judah** and Jerusalem. Use the same word or phrase for Judah as previously, and refer to Judah in the Master Glossary for more information.

The Israelites abandoned Yahweh's commands, which are Yahweh's laws and instructions.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **commands**. Look up **commandments** in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Yahweh gave commands to Yahweh's **servants**, the prophets. Although this is the same word for servant or slave that the storyteller used when he said that the Israelites were slaves, these prophets did not perform small tasks for Yahweh. Here, the storyteller uses the idea of a servant to show that the prophets did the things Yahweh asked them to do. Use the same word or phrase for servant as you used in previous passages. For more information on servant, refer to the Master Glossary.

Yahweh gave commands to his **prophets**. A prophet is a person who gives messages from God to the people. Use the same word or phrase for prophets as you used in previous passages. For more information on prophets, refer to the Master Glossary.

The Israelites were entering a land that the people had made unclean by the things they did that were unclean.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **unclean** or **polluted**. Use the same word or phrase that you used for unclean in Ezra 2:62\. Pause this audio here.

The people's **detestable practices** or **abominations** made the land impure. Use the same word or phrase for detestable practices or abominations as you used in previous passages.

Yahweh told the Israelites not to give their daughters in marriage to the sons of the Canaanite people. Marriage is the act in which two people marry each other. Marriage is also the relationship between two people who are married to each other.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **marriage**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Yahweh did not want the Israelites to make a treaty of friendship or to live in peace with the Canaanites.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for a **treaty of friendship**. Look up **peace** in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here

Yahweh wants to bless the Israelites with an everlasting inheritance or possession. Yahweh wants the Israelites to own the land and pass the land on to their descendants.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **inheritance**. Look up **heir** in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

What happened to the Israelites happened because of the Israelite's "evil deeds," actions which are bad and disobedient to God.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **evil deeds**. Look up **evil** in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this phrase in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Ezra asks if the Israelites will intermarry with foreign people. When people from different racial or religious groups "intermarry," they marry each other.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **intermarry**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Yahweh is the God of **Israel**. Use the same word or phrase for Israel as you used in previous passages. For more information on Israel, refer to the Master Glossary.

Yahweh is righteous. Everything Yahweh does is right and good.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **righteous**. Look up **righteousness** in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there.

Speaking the Word
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of the passage in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this session, retell the passage, as a group, in your own language.

First, the whole group should practice telling the passage in your own language. Remember to include the things you decided in previous steps, like chronology, words, phrases, emotions, or anything else you discussed.

One group member should tell a few sentences of the passage and pause. Another group member should tell the next part of the passage and pause. Do this until the group has retold the whole passage. The group members can correct each other in this step.

Pause this audio here.

Next, each member of the group should tell the whole passage without interruption at least one time. A group member can use random objects, motions, or their storyboard to help them remember the passage.

Pause this audio here.

Next, the group can decide whose version of the passage you like the most. You may decide that you liked the way one group member told one scene but you liked the way a different group member told another scene.

Pause this audio here.

Finally, the group can put together a final version of the passage that everyone agrees on. Each group member should practice telling this final version of the passage.

## Ezra 10:1–8 (id: eng-ezr-p20a-v1)

Hear and Heart
--------------

In this step, hear Ezra 10:1–8 and put it in your hearts.

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:1–8 three times, in three different translations, if possible.

Pause this audio here.

Now, as a group, discuss the following questions:

1. What do you like in this passage? Pause this audio here.
2. What do you not like or not understand in this passage? Pause this audio here.
3. What does this passage tell us about God? Pause this audio here.
4. What does this passage tell us about people? Pause this audio here.
5. How does this passage affect our daily lives? Pause this audio here.
6. Who do you know who needs to hear this passage?

Setting the Stage
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:1–8 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

This passage continues the story of Ezra in front of the temple in Jerusalem. The Israelite leaders told Ezra that the Israelites had disobeyed Yahweh, their God, because some of the Israelites had married women from the surrounding lands. The women are not Israelites and do not worship Yahweh. Ezra mourned and prayed for the people of Israel. The storyteller told us what Ezra prayed, and now, in this passage, the storyteller tells us how Ezra responds to the news from the leaders. Ezra prays to ask for help for the people of Israel. Ezra confesses the sins of the Israelites to God. Ezra shows signs of mourning by crying loudly and for a long time. Ezra prostrates himself. In other words, Ezra lay on the ground with his face down and forehead touching the ground. Ezra humbles himself in front of God. Ezra is in front of the house of God, the temple in Jerusalem.

Stop here and, as a group, look at a map of the temple in Jerusalem and find the open space in front of the temple. Pause this audio here.

The storyteller tells us that many people gather around Ezra before and during Ezra's prayer and mourning. The group of people is an "assembly," a special group of people who come together for a special purpose, usually related to worship of God.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Talk about a time when a large group of people came together to worship God. Now talk about a time when a large group of people came together for a different reason, maybe a wedding or other celebration. Notice what you call the group of people at these different times. Pause this audio here.

Men, women, and children gather around Ezra. The people are Israelites. The Israelite people also cry loudly and for a long time.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How do you and your people mourn or show great sadness? Pause this audio here.

Shecaniah, a man from the group of Israelites, talks to Ezra. Shecaniah's father was Jehiel. Shecaniah is part of the family group or clan of Elam. Elam was an ancestor of Shecaniah. Shecaniah speaks loudly and talks to the assembly as well as Ezra. Shecaniah says that the Israelites broke their oath to their God, and the Israelites are unfaithful. The Israelites married foreign women. The Israelite men asked the foreign women to live in the men's homes as the men's wives. The foreign women come from the land around Jerusalem, but these women are not Israelites. The foreign women worship different gods. Even though Shecaniah talks about the Israelites as if all of them were unfaithful, Shecaniah knows that only some Israelite men married foreign women.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Talk about men and women who live together in your community. What types of formal commitments do you have in your community between men and women? Pause this audio here.

You may remember from the book of Deuteronomy that Yahweh commanded the Israelites not to marry the people from the tribes that lived in and around Canaan.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Tell a story about a man who married a woman from a different country or culture from his own. Was the woman from a long way away or from people who live next to the man's country? Pause this audio here.

Shecaniah tells Ezra and the Israelite assembly that there is hope. Shecaniah believes something good will happen. Shecaniah wants the Israelites to make a covenant or solemn promise to each other in the presence of their God. Shecaniah wants the Israelites to promise to send the foreign women away from the Israelite homes. Shecaniah also wants the Israelites to promise to send away the children of the foreign women. Some Israelite men and the foreign women had children together. Shecaniah suggests this action because Shecaniah listened to the advice or counsel from Ezra and those Israelites who are strict followers of Yahweh. Shecaniah wants the Israelites to follow their God's commands or law. Shecaniah tells Ezra to make a start right now to send away the foreign women and children. Shecaniah trusts Ezra to make good decisions for the Israelites.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How do you encourage someone to quickly start to do something when the person feels scared and is frightened to start? Pause this audio here.

Ezra gets up to start to make the covenant with the assembly. Ezra makes a solemn promise with the leading priests, the Levite people, and all the Israelites at the assembly. The people promise Ezra that they will send away the foreign wives and their children. Ezra does not force the people to make the promise. Ezra walks away from the temple to a room or chamber nearby. The room was probably not part of the temple. The room may belong to Jehohanan, or the room may be named after Jehohanan. We do not know who Jehohanan is. Eliashib was the father of Jehohanan. Ezra uses the room during the night after he took the oaths of the people outside the temple. During the night after the events in the story, Ezra fasts and does not eat any food or drink any water. Ezra is very sad because the people who returned to Jerusalem from exile were not faithful to their God.

The Israelite leaders and elders make a proclamation. When someone speaks a proclamation, that person announces a message out loud to a group of people.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Talk about a time or times when a person spoke a proclamation to your people. How did the person speak it? Who spoke it? Pause this audio here.

The leaders' proclamation calls all the exiles, the people who have returned from Babylon, to gather as an assembly in Jerusalem. The leaders want all the men to come to Jerusalem. The men have three days to come to Jerusalem. The exiles lived close to Jerusalem, no further than three days' travel or 60 kilometers from Jerusalem.

Stop here and look at a map of Jerusalem and the lands of Judah and Benjamin. Look at the line around Jerusalem, which is 60 kilometers from Jerusalem. Pause this audio here.

Any Israelite man who does not come to Jerusalem will forfeit his property. In other words, the man will have to give up his property to the priests of the temple. The priests of the temple will own the man's property and may keep or destroy the property. The officials and elders will separate from the Israelites any man who does not come to Jerusalem. The officials and elders would not allow the man to join religious gatherings, and the Israelites would treat the man as a foreigner. You may remember that the Persian king gave authority to Ezra to make any decisions about the Israelites that Ezra needed to make. Even so, Ezra allowed the Israelite leaders to call the people and make the announcement.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: In your community, when can people in authority take away another person's property as a punishment? When might your community exclude someone from community events or a place of worship as a punishment?

Defining the Scenes
-------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:1–8 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will define the scenes, characters, and setting of this passage. Then the group will visualize this passage.

This passage has five scenes.

**In the first scene:** Ezra prays, confesses the Israelites' sins to God, cries, and prostrates himself in front of the temple. Israelites gather around Ezra and cry out loud.

**In the second scene:** Shecaniah speaks to Ezra and the Israelites. Shecaniah suggests the Israelites make a solemn promise to send away the foreign wives and their children and follow God's law. Shecaniah encourages Ezra to start the work.

**In the third scene:** Ezra makes the leading priests, Levites, and all the Israelites at the temple make a solemn promise to Ezra to send away the foreign wives and their children.

**In the fourth scene:** Ezra leaves the temple and goes to Jehohanan's room. Ezra does not eat or drink, and Ezra mourns because the exiles disobeyed God.

**In the fifth scene:** Israelite leaders and elders send a message to all the exiles in the land of Judah and Jerusalem to come to Jerusalem within three days. Any man who does not come will have to give his property to the temple, and the rest of the Israelite community will separate itself from the man.

The characters in this passage are:

* Ezra
* A large group of Israelites
* Shecaniah, son of Jehiel
* Leading priests, Levites, and Israelites
* Israelite leaders and elders
* And the exiles in Judah and Jerusalem

As a group, pay attention to these parts of the passage's setting:

The storyteller continues the story about when Ezra hears about Israelite men who married foreign women. In the last passage, the storyteller tells us Ezra's prayer to Yahweh, the Israelites' God. Now the storyteller goes back to telling the story. The storyteller reminds us of everything Ezra did between the time the leaders told Ezra about the Israelite men and Ezra's prayer at the end of the day. The storyteller also tells us about the people who came to be with Ezra while Ezra mourned and then prayed. The large group of people cried loudly and for a long time. These people are in addition to the people who trembled at the words of God, who were around Ezra when Ezra started to pray.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What words or phrases do you use to describe a group of people who are very sad and upset and cry loudly and for a long time? Pause this audio here.

Ezra and the large group of Israelite men, women, and children are in the open space in front of the house of God, the temple in Jerusalem.

Stop here and, as a group, look at a map of the temple in Jerusalem and find the open space in front of the temple, if needed. Pause this audio here.

Shecaniah, son of Jehiel, speaks to Ezra and to the Israelite people. Shecaniah's ancestor was Elam. Shecaniah agrees with Ezra that all the Israelites were unfaithful to God. Israelite men married foreign women, and the foreign women live in the homes of the Israelite men with their children.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What do you call people who come from a different culture or religion than you? Pause this audio here.

In the original language, Shecaniah does not use the normal words that the Israelites use to describe an Israelite marrying another Israelite. Shecaniah uses a different word, which the Israelites use to describe when an Israelite man takes a foreign woman into the Israelite man's home and lives with the woman as a wife for the Israelite man. Though these Israelite men considered and treated these foreign women as their wives, the Jewish law did not recognize these foreign women as legitimate wives.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How will you describe the relationship between an Israelite man and a foreign woman where the Israelite man treats the foreign woman like a wife? Pause this audio here.

Shecaniah thinks that there is hope for Israel, the people who follow Yahweh. Shecaniah thinks the people can be faithful to their God and survive as a people. Shecaniah wants the Israelite people to make a covenant, a solemn promise, in the presence of the Israelites' God. Shecaniah wants the people to promise to send away all the foreign women from the Israelite men's homes. When a man sends away a foreign woman, it is like he divorces the woman. However, it is not a formal divorce according to Jewish law because the Israelite man and the foreign woman were not married according to Jewish law. Shecaniah wants the Israelite men to send away the children of the Israelite men and the foreign women. Shecaniah claims that it is Ezra and the people who tremble at the commands of God who want the people to make the covenant to follow God's law and send away their wives and children. Shecaniah thinks that Ezra is a wise man, and Shecaniah thinks that Ezra has made a good proposal. Shecaniah wants Ezra's understanding of the Jewish law to guide the Israelites' response. Shecaniah encourages Ezra. Ezra is responsible for deciding what the Israelites will do. Shecaniah tells Ezra that Shecaniah and the other Israelites will support Ezra. Shecaniah tells Ezra to be brave and start doing something to help the Israelites.

Ezra moves from his place on the ground outside the temple. Ezra takes charge and leads the leading priests, Levites, and all the Israelite people around Ezra to make an official oath with God to send away the foreign women and their children. Everybody takes the oath.

After Ezra helps the Israelites make the oath to send away their foreign wives and children, Ezra leaves the open space in front of the temple and goes to a room. The room is near the temple in Jerusalem, in the living area for priests. In the room, Ezra continues to mourn and show great sadness that the exiles had disobeyed God. Ezra mourns through the night.

We do not know how much time passes between Ezra mourning in Jehohanan's room and the leaders and elders sending out a message to the exiles in Judah and Jerusalem. The elders and leaders want every Israelite man to come to Jerusalem within three days. The proclamation tells the people what will happen if someone does not obey the proclamation. A man who does not come to Jerusalem will have to give up all his possessions to the temple and will not be able to worship with the exiles.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What do you call an oral message from community leaders to your people? Pause this audio here.

Now, the group should storyboard, draw, or use objects to visualize the passage and the action in it.

Embodying the Text
------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:1–8 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will dramatize the passage.

This passage has five scenes.

The characters in this passage are:

* Ezra
* A large group of Israelites
* Shecaniah, son of Jehiel
* Leading priests, Levites, and Israelites
* Israelite leaders and elders
* And the exiles in Judah and Jerusalem

As a group, act out the passage twice. You should act out the passage in your own language.

First, act out the passage without stopping. Pay attention to the dialogue, flow, plotline, and chronology of the passage. Make sure you do not skip acting out the difficult or important parts of the passage. Help each other remember every part of the passage.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage.

The group should act out this passage a second time. At certain points in the drama, pause the drama and ask the person playing the character, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person playing the character should answer what they would be feeling or thinking if they were that character. Then continue the drama.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage a second time.

The following is an example of the drama and possible responses.

Ezra prays, confesses the Israelites' sins to God, cries, and prostrates himself in front of the temple. Israelites gather around Ezra and cry out loud.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Will Yahweh kill all of us now? or
* We have been unfaithful to Yahweh and not followed Yahweh's commands to us; or
* I am so upset. Yahweh, please forgive us.

Ask the person playing Yahweh, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* My people have been unfaithful; or
* I hear Ezra, my servant; or
* Many of my people are sad today. My people know that I will judge my people.

Ask the person playing the large group of Israelites, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Yahweh will punish us; or
* We are worried and frightened. Will we lose our land again? or
* Ezra mourns for us. Ezra must care about us.

Continue the drama.

Shecaniah speaks to Ezra and the Israelites. Shecaniah suggests the Israelites make a solemn promise to send away the foreign wives and their children and follow God's law. Shecaniah encourages Ezra to start the work.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Shecaniah, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I know what we can do to please Yahweh; or
* I want to help Ezra and my people. Maybe Yahweh will have mercy on us; or
* Let us do something now, Ezra. We can promise to send the foreign women and children away.

Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Shecaniah is right; or
* I feel hope for us; or
* Shecaniah will help me. I feel better now.

Ask the person playing the large group of Israelites, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Shecaniah is right; or
* We feel very sad. It will be hard to send away the foreign women and their young children from our homes; or
* We can make a promise today.

Continue the drama.

Ezra makes the leading priests, Levites, and all the Israelites outside the temple make a solemn promise to Ezra to send away the foreign wives and their children.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I am relieved. We are making a good decision today; or
* Yahweh sees our promise; or
* I hope Yahweh forgives us.

Ask the person playing leading priests, Levites, and Israelites, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* It feels good to make this promise to Ezra; or
* Will Yahweh forgive us? or
* We need to make sure we know which women and children to send away.

Continue the drama.

Ezra leaves the temple and goes to Jehohanan's room. Ezra does not eat or drink, and Ezra mourns because the exiles disobeyed God.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I am so sad; or
* I am worried about the Israelites who came back from Babylon; or
* Yahweh, please forgive us.

Continue the drama.

Israelite leaders and elders send a message to all the exiles in the land of Judah and Jerusalem to come to Jerusalem within three days. Any man who does not come will have to give his property to the temple, and the rest of the Israelite community will separate itself from the man.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Israelite leaders and elders, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We need to keep our promise to send away the foreign women and the children; or
* We hope every man comes to Jerusalem; or
* We hope this will stop Yahweh from destroying us.

Ask the person playing the exiles in Judah and Jerusalem, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* All our men must go to Jerusalem; or
* We need to be obedient to our leaders and to Yahweh; or
* We do not want the priests to take our belongings. We want to be part of the people of Israel.

Filling the Gaps
----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:1–8 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will discuss key terms and words in this passage.

Ezra **prays** and confesses to Yahweh. Ezra knows the Israelites were disobedient to God and tells God about all the wrong things the Israelites did. Use the same word or phrase for pray as you used in previous passages, and refer to the Master Glossary for more information if needed.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for "**confesses**." If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here

Ezra **weeps**. Ezra is very sad and cries loudly and for a long time. Use the same word or phrase for weeps as you used in previous passages.

Ezra is in front of the **house of God**. Ezra is in front of the temple in Jerusalem. Use the same words or phrases for "house of God" and God as you used in previous passages. For more information on "house of God," temple, and God, refer to the Master Glossary.

A great assembly of men, women, and children from Israel, or "**Israelites**," gathered around Ezra. Use the same word or phrase for Israelites as you used in previous passages. For more information on Israelites, refer to the Master Glossary.

An assembly is a group of people who gather together for a particular purpose.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **assembly**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Shecaniah is a **descendant** of Elam. Use the same word or phrase for descendant as you used in previous passages. For more information on descendant, refer to the Master Glossary.

Shecaniah says the Israelites have been **unfaithful** to God. Use the same word or phrase for unfaithful as you used in previous passages.

Some Israelites married foreign women. The foreign women are the wives of Israelites and live in the homes of the Israelites. The married relationship between the foreign woman and the Israelite man is not an official marriage.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **married** in this story. Pause this audio here.

Some Israelites married foreign women. The women are not Israelites and come from outside the Israelite community. The storyteller uses a word for foreign that is not very positive. These are the kinds of foreigners that do not belong in a place.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **foreign**, or a foreign person who does not belong in that place. Pause this audio here.

Shecaniah has hope for **Israel**, the people of Israel. Shecaniah feels that he can trust God that something good will happen to the people of Israel. Use the same word or phrase for Israel as you have previously, and refer to Israel in the Master Glossary for more information.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **hope**. Look up hope in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Shecaniah wants the Israelites to make a covenant, which is a solemn promise.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **covenant**. Look up covenant in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Shecaniah wants the Israelites to follow the Law. The Law usually refers to all the commands that Yahweh gave to Moses. Although there is no law of Moses that says an Israelite must send away a foreign wife, the law does say that Israelites are not supposed to marry wives from the lands near them. And, the law states that an Israelite man can divorce a wife who does not please the man.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **Law**. Look up law in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

Ezra makes the **leading priests** and **Levites** take an oath. These men are leaders among the priests and the Levites. Use the same words or phrases for leading priests and Levites as you used in previous passages. For more information on priests and Levites, refer to the Master Glossary.

The people took the oath. The people made a very serious promise in the presence of Yahweh.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **oath**. Look up oath in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

The leaders made a **proclamation** for the **exiles** to come together in Jerusalem. The leaders gave a loud, spoken, formal message to the people who returned from Babylon. Use the same words or phrases for proclamation and exiles as you used in previous passages.

A person who does not come to Jerusalem will forfeit all their property. The property will no longer belong to the person.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **forfeit**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

The **officials** and **elders** will decide if anybody has to forfeit their property. Use the same words or phrases for officials and elders as you used in previous passages. For more information on elders, refer to the Master Glossary.

Speaking the Word
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of the passage in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this session, retell the passage, as a group, in your own language.

First, the whole group should practice telling the passage in your own language. Remember to include the things you decided in previous steps, like chronology, words, phrases, emotions, or anything else you discussed.

One group member should tell a few sentences of the passage and pause. Another group member should tell the next part of the passage and pause. Do this until the group has retold the whole passage. The group members can correct each other in this step.

Pause this audio here.

Next, each member of the group should tell the whole passage without interruption at least one time. A group member can use random objects, motions, or their storyboard to help them remember the passage.

Pause this audio here.

Next, the group can decide whose version of the passage you like the most. You may decide that you liked the way one group member told one scene but you liked the way a different group member told another scene.

Pause this audio here.

Finally, the group can put together a final version of the passage that everyone agrees on. Each group member should practice telling this final version of the passage.
