## Ezra 10:9–17 (id: eng-ezr-p20b-v1)

Hear and Heart
--------------

In this step, hear Ezra 10:9–17 and put it in your hearts.

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:9–17 three times, in three different translations, if possible.

Pause this audio here.

Now, as a group, discuss the following questions:

1. What do you like in this passage? Pause this audio here.
2. What do you not like or not understand in this passage? Pause this audio here.
3. What does this passage tell us about God? Pause this audio here.
4. What does this passage tell us about people? Pause this audio here.
5. How does this passage affect our daily lives? Pause this audio here.
6. Who do you know who needs to hear this passage?

Setting the Stage
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:9–17 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this story, we hear what happens when the people assemble in Jerusalem. The story continues on from the previous story. At the end of the previous story, the Israelite leaders and elders sent out a proclamation to all the Israelites in the areas of Judah and Jerusalem. The Israelite leaders and elders told the Israelite men to come to Jerusalem. The men have three days to come to Jerusalem.

The Israelites obey Ezra's proclamation. All the Jewish men who live in the lands Yahweh gave to Judah and Benjamin arrive in Jerusalem. On the twentieth day of the ninth month in the year, the people gather and wait in the open space in front of the temple.

Stop here and, as a group, look at a map of the temple in Jerusalem. Find the open space in front of the temple. Pause this audio here.

In Ezra's time, there were usually 12 months in a year. The ninth month was at the beginning of colder weather. In Jerusalem at this time of year, the weather was often cold with lots of rain.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How does the weather change in your area through the year? What time of year is colder? What time of year do you have more rain? Pause this audio here.

The people in the open space were very unhappy. The people were trembling because of worry and fear about what Ezra might say or what their God might do to them. The people were also trembling because they were cold and wet. Ezra told the men that they had broken God's command because the men married foreign women. These men's sins increased Israel's guilt. The men's sins were in addition to the sins of Israel that made God allow the Babylonians to exile the Israelites many years ago. Ezra wants the men to give honor, thanks, and respect to Yahweh and do what pleases Yahweh. Ezra tells the Israelite men to be separate from the people who do not follow Yahweh and from their foreign wives.

All the men in front of the temple call out to answer Ezra. The men say that Ezra is right and that the Israelite men have to do what Ezra said to the men. Some Israelite men then give reasons why the Israelite men cannot do what Ezra wants on that day. We do not know which men speak to Ezra. The Israelite men say that there are too many men for the elders to make a judgement about in one day. The Israelite men also say that on that day, it is raining too much for the men to stand outside to consider each man with a foreign wife. The storyteller then tells us that the Israelites cannot take care of the problem in a day or two because the Israelites have sinned a lot by taking foreign wives. The Israelite men are probably saying that this is too important a matter to consider quickly and too complicated to make a general solution for everyone. When the men say that it is too important to deal with "in a day or two," the men are probably talking about an unknown length of time as opposed to exactly one or two days. The people in the assembly propose to Ezra a way to carry out Ezra's instructions to the Israelites. The men propose that leaders or officials in the Israelite community do the work of the assembly. The men propose that the leaders set a time in each town for a meeting between men married to foreign women and the elders and judges of the town. At the meeting, the elders and judges will consider the marriage and make a decision. The elders are respected and responsible members of the Israelite community. The judges are Israelite men who support and maintain the laws of the community and help to organise the community.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What do you call the people in your community who help to organise and lead your community and make sure people follow the laws of your community? Pause this audio here.

The Israelite elders and judges will work until the elders and judges judge every man, and the Israelite men are separate from the foreign women and their children. When the Israelites finish the action, God will stop being very angry with the Israelites for marrying foreign wives.

The storyteller tells us that Jonathan, son of Asahel, and Jahzeiah, son of Tikvah, disagreed with the assembly's proposal. Asahel is the father of Jonathan, and Tikvah is the father of Jahzeiah. We do not know why Jonathan and Jahzeiah disagreed with the proposal. It is possible that the two men do not want to give up their foreign wives, or alternatively, the two men may not want to wait for a decision about their marriages. Meshullam and Shabbethai the Levite supported Jonathan and Jahzeiah. We do not know if these men agreed with Jonathan and Jahzeiah or if they agreed with the proposal. Meshullam may be the same Meshullam who traveled with Ezra to Jerusalem. Shabbethai may be the leader of the Levites that the storyteller of Nehemiah tells us about.

The storyteller tells us that the exiles, the Israelites who returned from Babylon to Jerusalem, followed the plan the Israelite men proposed to Ezra outside the temple in Jerusalem. Ezra chose men who were leaders of the clans, the family groups. Ezra named each person whom Ezra chose to investigate each case or situation of marriage. The leaders started to investigate and find out the truth about the marriages of Israelite men on the first day of the tenth month. This day was ten days after the assembly at the temple in Jerusalem. The leaders finished their work by the first day of the first month of the next year. It took the leaders three months to decide what to do in all the situations where Israelite men married foreign wives.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Talk about a time someone investigated or looked for the truth in a difficult or complicated situation in your community or in your family. Who investigated the situation? How long did it take the person to find out what happened?

Defining the Scenes
-------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:9–17 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will define the scenes, characters, and setting of this passage. Then the group will visualize this passage.

This passage has four scenes.

**In the first scene:** For three days, the Israelite men who live in the areas of Judah and Benjamin travel from their homes to Jerusalem.

**In the second scene:** The Israelite men from the areas of Judah and Benjamin wait in the open space in front of the temple. The Israelite men are worried and uncomfortable because they do not know what will happen, and they are cold and wet. Ezra tells the Israelite men that they were unfaithful to God and even more guilty now than they were before. The Israelite men must live separately from the people who are not Israelites, and the Israelite men must send away the foreign wives of the Israelites. The Israelite men agree and propose a plan to judge what each man with a foreign wife should do. Some men did not agree with what the people said in the open space in front of the temple.

**In the third scene:** Ezra chooses leaders from the Israelite clans to consider each situation of an Israelite man married to a foreign woman.

**In the fourth scene:** For three months, the community leaders investigate all the Israelite men with foreign wives and make decisions for the Israelite men.

The characters in this passage are:

* All the Israelite men from Judah and Benjamin, including the men who had married foreign women
* Ezra
* Jonathan, Jahzeiah, Meshullam, and Shabbethai
* And heads of Israelite family groups

As a group, pay attention to these parts of the passage's setting:

In the previous story, the leaders and elders sent out a proclamation to call the Israelite men in Judah and Jerusalem to meet in Jerusalem. This story starts three days after the end of the previous story. The Israelites hear the proclamation, and the men go to Jerusalem. All the men go to Jerusalem during the three days after the proclamation.

All the men go to the open space in front of the temple on the twentieth day of the ninth month. We do not know if this is the third day after the proclamation or the next day after the third day. The men gather and wait in the square. The square was an open area within a city or group of buildings. In this case, this is the area in front of the temple. We do not know if everyone is sitting down or if some are sitting and some are standing.

Stop here and, as a group, look at a map of the temple in Jerusalem. Find the open space in front of the temple, if needed. Pause this audio here.

All the men trembled or shivered. The storyteller makes it clear that the men trembled for two reasons. The men trembled because they were worried, and the men trembled because they were cold and wet from the rain.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What do you call cold rain that makes people very wet and lasts a long time? Pause this audio here.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How will you make it clear in your translation that the men trembled for two reasons? Pause this audio here.

The storyteller reminds us that Ezra is a priest. Ezra speaks to the men in front of the temple and tells the men what they have done wrong. Ezra uses many of the same words and phrases that Ezra used in earlier passages. The men took foreign women as wives into their homes. Ezra tells the men that they have increased Israel's guilt. The people of Israel are more deserving of God's judgement and punishment than before. Ezra wants the men to admit to Yahweh what the men have done wrong and do what Yahweh wants them to do. Ezra wants the men to be separate from the people from the surrounding lands who are not Israelites. Ezra also wants the men to send away their foreign wives.

Everyone in the assembly replies to Ezra with a loud voice. The people agree with Ezra.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Have one person stand apart from the group. Have the rest of the group stand together and say together "Yes" and "We agree." Afterward, talk about how your voices sounded when you spoke together. Pause this audio here.

Some people speak to suggest a plan to Ezra. The men know it will take a long time to look at every relationship between an Israelite man and a foreign woman. There are too many relationships for Ezra to look at on his own. People cannot stay outside because it is cold and wet. The Israelite men know it is important to make everything right because the Israelite men know many people are disobeying Yahweh.

The men in the assembly suggest to Ezra a way to find all the men who have foreign women in their homes as wives. The assembly wants officials to do the work for all the Israelite men. The elders and judges of each town will set times to meet with men who have married foreign women. The elders and judges will meet with men until they are finished so that God's anger will turn away from the Israelites. The Israelite men use special language to describe God's very strong anger at the Israelites. God's anger is fierce, just like something hot or burning.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What words or phrases do you use to describe a person's intense and strong anger toward a person or people? Pause this audio here.

Jonathan and Jahzeiah opposed what the people said. Meshullam and Shabbethai supported Jonathan and Jahzeiah. We do not know what Jonathan and Jahzeiah oppose. The men may not want to separate from their foreign wives, or the men may not want the elders and judges to judge each marriage so slowly.

The storyteller finishes the story by telling us that the exiles, the Israelites who came back from Babylon with Zerubbabel and afterward, followed the plan from the assembly. Ezra chooses men who are heads of families. Ezra chooses one man from each family division or clan and names the men. The storyteller tells us that the chosen men started to investigate the cases, the situations of men with foreign wives. The men started to work on the first day of the tenth month. The men finished all the cases by the first day of the first month of the following year. The men took three months to investigate all the cases.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How will you translate the time the Israelites took to investigate all the cases? Pause this audio here.

Now, the group should storyboard, draw, or use objects to visualize the passage and the action in it.

Embodying the Text
------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:9–17 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will dramatize the passage.

This passage has four scenes.

The characters in this passage are:

* All the Israelite men from Judah and Benjamin, including the men who had married foreign women
* Ezra
* Jonathan, Jahzeiah, Meshullam, and Shabbethai
* And heads of Israelite family groups

As a group, act out the passage twice. You should act out the passage in your own language.

First, act out the passage without stopping. Pay attention to the dialogue, flow, plotline, and chronology of the passage. Make sure you do not skip acting out the difficult or important parts of the passage. Help each other remember every part of the passage.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage.

The group should act out this passage a second time. At certain points in the drama, pause the drama and ask the person playing the character, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person playing the character should answer what they would be feeling or thinking if they were that character. Then continue the drama.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage a second time.

The following is an example of the drama and possible responses.

For three days, the Israelite men who live in Judah and Benjamin travel from their homes to Jerusalem.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing all the Israelite men from Judah and Benjamin, including the men who had married foreign women, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* This is important. We must go to Jerusalem; or
* We are worried. Some of us have made Yahweh angry; or
* There are so many men in Jerusalem. Everyone listened to our leaders.

Continue the drama.

The Israelite men from Judah and Benjamin wait in the open space in front of the temple. The men are worried and uncomfortable because they do not know what will happen, and the men are cold and wet. Ezra tells the men the Israelite men were unfaithful to God and even more guilty now than they were before. The Israelite men must live separately from the people who are not Israelites, and the Israelite men must send away the foreign wives of the Israelites. The Israelite men agree and propose a plan to consider each man with a foreign wife. Some men did not agree with what the people said in the square.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing all the men of Judah and Benjamin, including the men who had married foreign women, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We are cold and wet. This is a terrible time of the year to stand outside in front of the temple; or
* Ezra tells us the truth. We need to do something; or
* Yahweh is angry with us. Yahweh may kill us all or make us leave Jerusalem again; or
* We need wise people in our community to look at each marriage of an Israelite to a foreign woman.

Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I want everybody to understand that Israel is in danger; or
* I am so worried and frightened for us; or
* Now every Israelite man must be faithful to Yahweh and not have a foreign wife; or
* We need a plan to stop Yahweh's anger at us.

Ask the person playing Jonathan, Jahzeiah, Meshullam, and Shabbethai, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Will we separate ourselves from the foreign wives in time to stop Yahweh from punishing us? or
* We do not know if this is the right plan to stop Yahweh's anger; or
* We are worried about the plan.

Continue the drama.

Ezra chooses leaders from the Israelite clans to judge each situation of an Israelite man with a foreign wife.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing Ezra, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* These are wise men. The Israelite community trusts these men; or
* Now everybody will know which men will look at the cases of Israelite men married to foreign wives; or
* I feel relief. Yahweh will be pleased with us.

Ask the person playing heads of Israelite family groups, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Ezra chose us to make good decisions; or
* We need to look at all the information to make a good decision; or
* There is a lot of work for us. We are happy to do the work to stop Yahweh's anger.

Continue the drama.

For three months, the community leaders investigate all the Israelite men with foreign wives and make decisions for the Israelite men.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing heads of Israelite family groups, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We must listen to all the information to make a good decision; or
* The men in our community trust us to do a good job; or
* We must keep going until we have looked at every case.

Ask the person playing all the men of Judah and Benjamin, including the men who had married foreign women, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We trust our elders to listen to us and make the right decision for us; or
* We are sad. We made a bad decision to marry foreign women. We made Yahweh angry; or
* We will miss our wives and children.

Filling the Gaps
----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:9–17 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will discuss key terms and words in this passage.

All the men from the areas of **Judah** and Benjamin gathered in Jerusalem. Use the same words or phrases for Judah and Jerusalem as you used in previous passages. For more information on Judah, refer to the Master Glossary.

The people sat in the square. A square is a flat, open space where people can gather. A square is usually surrounded by buildings.

Stop here and, as a group, look at a map of the temple in Jerusalem. Find the open space, the square, in front of the temple, if needed. Pause this audio here.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **square**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

The people sat in front of the **house of God**. Use the same word or phrase for house of God as you used in previous passages. Refer to "house of God" and temple in the Master Glossary for more information.

Ezra the **priest** stood up and told the men that the men had been **unfaithful**. Use the same words or phrases for priest and unfaithful as you used in previous passages. For more information about priest, refer to the Master Glossary.

The Israelite men **married** **foreign** women. The Israelite men and foreign women had formal relationships like marriage but not an official marriage. The word here is not the usual word to use for marry because the marriages were not official marriages. Use the same words or phrases for married and foreign as you used in previous passages.

The Israelite men added to **Israel**'s **guilt**. Use the same words or phrases for Israel and guilt as you used in previous passages. For more information on Israel and guilt, refer to the Master Glossary.

Ezra tells the men to make a confession to **Yahweh**. Yahweh is the personal name for God. Be sure to translate Yahweh in the same way as you have in previous passages, and remember that Yahweh is in the Master Glossary.

Yahweh is the **God** of the Israelite's **ancestors**. Use the same words or phrases for God and ancestors as you used in previous passages. For more information on God, refer to the Master Glossary.

The **assembly**, or group of Israelites, responded to Ezra. Use the same word or phrase for assembly as you used in previous passages.

The people in the assembly say that they have transgressed against Yahweh. A transgression is like a sin. When someone "transgresses" or does something wrong towards Yahweh or another person, the person causes great offense to that person.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **transgression**. For more information about transgression, refer to the Master Glossary. Pause this audio here.

The Israelite men want Israelite **officials** to act for the whole assembly. Use the same word or phrase for officials as you used in previous passages.

The **elders** and **judges** of each town will meet with men who married foreign women. An elder is a person with authority in a community. A judge is a person in the community who makes judgements and decisions about the law. Use the same words or phrases for elders and judges as you have in previous passages, and refer to elder and judge in the Master Glossary for more information.

Use the same word for **town** as you used in previous passages. Here, town is a general word for a settlement of people of any size, from very small to a big city with walls around it.

The **exiles** did what the Israelite men proposed. Use the same word or phrase for exiles as you used in previous passages.

Ezra chose men who were "**family heads**" or leaders. Use the same word or phrase for family heads as you used in previous passages.

Speaking the Word
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of the passage in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this session, retell the passage, as a group, in your own language.

First, the whole group should practice telling the passage in your own language. Remember to include the things you decided in previous steps, like chronology, words, phrases, emotions, or anything else you discussed.

One group member should tell a few sentences of the passage and pause. Another group member should tell the next part of the passage and pause. Do this until the group has retold the whole passage. The group members can correct each other in this step.

Pause this audio here.

Next, each member of the group should tell the whole passage without interruption at least one time. A group member can use random objects, motions, or their storyboard to help them remember the passage.

Pause this audio here.

Next, the group can decide whose version of the passage you like the most. You may decide that you liked the way one group member told one scene but you liked the way a different group member told another scene.

Pause this audio here.

Finally, the group can put together a final version of the passage that everyone agrees on. Each group member should practice telling this final version of the passage.

* **Associated Passages:** Ezra 10:9-17

* **Associated ACAI Concepts:** LORD (ID: `deity:Lord`); Ezra (ID: `person:Ezra`); Shabbethai (ID: `person:Shabbethai`); Jahzeiah (ID: `person:Jahzeiah`); Jonathan (ID: `person:Jonathan.10`); Asahel (ID: `person:Asahel.4`); Meshullam (ID: `person:Meshullam.10`); Tikvah (ID: `person:Tikvah.2`); Tribe of Levi (ID: `group:Levi`); Judah (ID: `person:Judah.4`); Tribe of Benjamin (ID: `group:Benjamin`); Jerusalem (ID: `place:Jerusalem`); Praise (ID: `keyterm:Praise`); Tribe of Judah (ID: `group:Judah`); Israel (ID: `person:Israel`); Delight (ID: `keyterm:Delight`); Strength (ID: `keyterm:Strength`); Be Unfaithful (ID: `keyterm:Unfaithful`); Rebel (ID: `keyterm:Rebel`); Levi (ID: `person:Levi.3`); Benjamin (ID: `person:Benjamin`); House (ID: `realia:House`)

## Ezra 10:18–24 (id: eng-ezr-p21a-v1)

Hear and Heart
--------------

In this step, hear Ezra 10:18–24 and put it in your hearts.

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:18–24 three times, in three different translations, if possible.

Pause this audio here.

Now, as a group, discuss the following questions:

1. What do you like in this passage? Pause this audio here.
2. What do you not like or not understand in this passage? Pause this audio here.
3. What does this passage tell us about God? Pause this audio here.
4. What does this passage tell us about people? Pause this audio here.
5. How does this passage affect our daily lives? Pause this audio here.
6. Who do you know who needs to hear this passage?

Setting the Stage
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:18–24 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this story and the next story, the storyteller ends the story about Ezra and the Israelites with foreign wives. You will remember that some Israelite men took foreign women, women who were not Israelite, into their homes. The Israelite men lived with the women in the same way as an Israelite man married and lived with an Israelite woman. Ezra knew that some Israelite men had disobeyed Yahweh and married foreign women. Ezra and the Israelite leaders agreed to judge the Israelite men and make sure the Israelite men separated themselves from their foreign wives.

In this story, the storyteller tells us which Israelite men married foreign women. The storyteller starts with a list of Israelite men who are the sons or descendants of priests. You will remember that Yahweh set apart the Levite tribe to serve Yahweh. In the Levite tribe, Yahweh chose some people to be Yahweh's priests. The men descended from Yahweh's priests served Yahweh as priests from one generation to the next. The priests were important religious leaders.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What families or people in your community or country, if any, are important, special, or set apart for special work? How do ordinary people expect the special people to behave? How do the laws of your people apply to the special people? Pause this audio here.

In the time of Zerubbabel, a man named Jeshua, also known as Joshua, was the high priest in Jerusalem. You will remember that the storyteller identifies families of men by an important ancestor. In this story, the storyteller uses Jeshua as the important ancestor for the men descended from the high priest. Jeshua's father was Jozadak. In some translations, the storyteller calls Jozadak "Jehozadak." You may remember from Ezra 2:36 that the storyteller identifies this Jeshua as from the larger family of Jedaiah. In this part of the story in Ezra, the storyteller uses this Jeshua to identify the family because Jeshua was an important person. Jeshua led the family back to Jerusalem from Babylon.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How do you identify different family groups in your community? Is there a connection between the way you identify family groups and significant ancestors in the families? Pause this audio here.

The storyteller tells us that the first group of men is from Jeshua's family and Jeshua's brothers. The storyteller may not mean brothers who have the same father and mother as Jeshua. The storyteller uses the word "brothers" to mean other priests who are related by blood to Jeshua and are part of Jeshua's wider family.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Talk about people who are part of your wider family. The wider family is the people you are related to by blood but do not have the same father and mother as you. Pay attention to how you describe your wider family. Pause this audio here.

Maaseiah, Eliezer, Jarib, and Gedaliah were male descendants of Jeshua. You will remember that it was common to call male descendants the sons of a significant ancestor. The storyteller tells us that these men gave their hands as a pledge or promise to separate from their wives. The storyteller does not mean that the men actually gave their hands to somebody. At the time of Ezra, a person shook or held hands with another person to show their promise to that person.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What things do you do to make a strong agreement or promise with someone? Pause this audio here.

The storyteller also tells us that Maaseiah, Eliezer, Jarib, and Gedaliah each gave a ram to the temple for the priests to sacrifice as a guilt offering. A ram is an adult male sheep.

Stop here and look at a picture of a ram as a group. Pause this audio here.

The ram came from the group or flock of sheep that the Israelites kept for sacrifices. The men gave the rams for sacrifice because the men had broken Yahweh's law. You may remember that an Israelite person would make this offering whether the person purposely or accidentally disobeyed a law. The Israelite men at the time of Ezra did not know Yahweh's law very well. The Israelite men probably did not mean to be unfaithful to Yahweh when the men took foreign women as wives. It is not clear from the story whether all the Israelite men who were guilty of marrying foreign women made guilt offerings. It is possible that only Maaseiah, Eliezer, Jarib, and Gedaliah made sacrifices. However, Yahweh's law taught the Israelites that everyone who broke Yahweh's law should make a guilt offering to Yahweh.

The storyteller continues the list of guilty men by telling us about the other priest families. In the family of Immer, Hanani and Zebadiah were guilty. In the family of Harim, Maaseiah, Elijah, Shemaiah, Jehiel, and Uzziah were guilty. In the family of Pashhur, Elioenai, Maaseiah, Ishmael, Nethanel, Jozabad, and Elasah were guilty. Immer, Harim, and Pashhur were not alive at the time of this story. Immer, Harim, and Pashhur are the significant ancestors in these three other priest families. You will notice that there are men with the same names in different families. The repeated names in the different families are different people who share a common name. We do not know anything about the men in the list.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What are some common names that people give to more than one person in your community? Pause this audio here.

Next, the storyteller tells us about the Levite men who were not priests but who are also guilty. The storyteller tells us of a group of six Levite men who are guilty, but does not tell us which family or families these men come from. However, the men are probably descendants of Jeshua and Kadmiel. The six Levite men are Jozabad, Shimei, Kelaiah, also known as Kelita, Pethahiah, Judah, and Eliezer. Earlier in the book of Ezra, the storyteller told us that Jozabad received the gifts for the temple from Ezra. Also, the storyteller of Nehemiah tells us that Jozabad and Kelita helped to explain the Law. We also know from Nehemiah that Jozabad was a Levite leader who supervised the people who worked on the outside of the temple. The storyteller of Nehemiah 10:10 also tells us that Kelita put his name on the written covenant.

The next person comes from the group of Levites who are musicians or singers. You will remember that the musicians are the descendants of Asaph, who sing and make music in the temple. Eliashib the musician was guilty.

The last group of Levites who were guilty were from the gatekeepers. The gatekeepers were people responsible for guarding the temple and the entrances of the temple. The gatekeepers took care of the rooms and the valuable objects in the temple. The gatekeepers were not soldiers. Shallum, Telem, and Uri from the gatekeepers were guilty.

Defining the Scenes
-------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:18–24 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will define the scenes, characters, and setting of this passage. Then the group will visualize this passage.

This passage has five scenes.

**In the first scene:** The storyteller introduces the list of guilty men and tells us the four guilty men from the family of Jeshua, son of Jozadak. The men are Levite priests.

**In the second scene:** The storyteller tells us that the guilty men promise to separate themselves from their wives and each give a ram as a guilt offering.

**In the third scene:** The storyteller tells us the two guilty men who are descendants of Immer, the five guilty men who are descendants of Harim, and the six guilty men who are descendants of Pashhur. All the men are Levite priests.

**In the fourth scene:** The storyteller tells us six more Levite men who are guilty.

**In the fifth scene:** The storyteller tells us that one man from the musician Levites is guilty and that three men from the gatekeeper Levites are guilty.

The characters in this passage are:

* Storyteller
* The guilty Levite priest descendants of Jeshua: Maaseiah, Eliezer, Jarib, and Gedaliah
* The guilty Levite priest descendants of Immer: Hanani and Zebadiah
* The guilty Levite priest descendants of Harim: Maaseiah, Elijah, Shemaiah, Jehiel, and Uzziah
* The guilty Levite priest descendants of Pashhur: Elioenai, Maaseiah, Ishmael, Nethanel, Jozabad, and Elasah
* The guilty Levites: Jozabad, Shimei, Kelaiah, Pethahiah, Judah and Eliezer
* The guilty musician, Eliashib
* And the guilty gatekeepers: Shallum, Telem, and Uri

As a group, pay attention to these parts of the passage's setting:

This story continues from the previous passage when the Israelites decided which men had foreign wives. The storyteller finishes the story now by telling us a list of the men who broke Yahweh's law and were guilty. The storyteller starts the list by telling us about the men from Levite priest families, the important religious leaders of the community. The storyteller divides the list into groups of men according to the family each man belongs to. Each family group is identified as the descendants or sons of an important ancestor. The first group of men is the descendants of Jeshua and Jeshua's brothers or close family. The guilty men are Maaseiah, Eliezer, Jarib, and Gedaliah.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: What words do you use to describe people who are related to each other by blood? Think about words that indicate a specific relationship as well as words that are more general. Pause this audio here.

The storyteller pauses the list to tell us that the guilty men gave their hands as a promise to send away their wives. You will remember that this is special language that means the men held or shook another person's hand with their own hand.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: How do you say someone has made an agreement with, or a promise to, another person to do something? Pause this audio here.

The storyteller also tells us that each man brought a ram to the priests at the temple to make a guilt offering.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together four small objects and place them in a group in front of you. The four objects represent the four guilty men. Now find four more small objects. These objects represent the four rams that the men bring to the priests for the sacrifice. Place these objects in front of you and take away the other objects to represent how the rams take the punishment for the guilt of these men. Pause this audio here.

The storyteller returns to the list of guilty men who were Levite priests. The next group of men are descendants of Immer. The guilty men are Hanani and Zebadiah.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together two more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The next group of men are descendants of Harim. The guilty men are Maaseiah, Elijah, Shemaiah, Jehiel, and Uzziah.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together five more small objects. Like before, place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activities before this one. Pause this audio here.

The last group of Levite priests is descendants of Pashhur. The guilty men are Elioenai, Maaseiah, Ishmael, Nethanel, Jozabad, and Elasah.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together six more small objects. Like before, place these objects together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activities before this one. Pause this audio here.

The storyteller now tells us about other groups of Levite men who are guilty. The storyteller does not tell us the family or families of the men in the first group of Levites who are not priests. The guilty Levite men are Jozabad, Shimei, Kelaiah, who is also known as Kelita, Pethahiah, Judah, and Eliezer.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together six more small objects. Place these objects together in a group near the other groups of objects. Leave a bigger space between these objects and the groups of objects from the activities before this one to show that these men are Levites but are not priests. Pause this audio here.

The next group of men is temple musicians or singers. There is only one guilty musician. The man is called Eliashib.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect one small object. Place this object next to but separate from the group of six objects in the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The last group of Levite men in the list is the gatekeepers for the temple. The guilty men are Shallum, Telem, and Uri.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together three more small objects. Like before, place the objects together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects in the activity before this one. Notice all the different objects that represent all the guilty Levite men. Pause this audio here.

Now, the group should storyboard, draw, or use objects to visualize the passage and the action in it.

Embodying the Text
------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:18–24 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will dramatize the passage.

This passage has five scenes.

The characters in this passage are:

* Storyteller
* The guilty Levite priest descendants of Jeshua: Maaseiah, Eliezer, Jarib, and Gedaliah
* The guilty Levite priest descendants of Immer: Hanani and Zebadiah
* The guilty Levite priest descendants of Harim: Maaseiah, Elijah, Shemaiah, Jehiel, and Uzziah
* The guilty Levite priest descendants of Pashhur: Elioenai, Maaseiah, Ishmael, Nethanel, Jozabad, and Elasah
* The guilty Levites: Jozabad, Shimei, Kelaiah, Pethahiah, Judah, and Eliezer
* The guilty musician, Eliashib
* And the guilty gatekeepers: Shallum, Telem, and Uri

As a group, act out the passage twice. You should act out the passage in your own language.

First, act out the passage without stopping. Pay attention to the dialogue, flow, plotline, and chronology of the passage. Make sure you do not skip acting out the difficult or important parts of the passage. Help each other remember every part of the passage.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage.

The group should act out this passage a second time. At certain points in the drama, pause the drama and ask the person playing the character, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person playing the character should answer what they would be feeling or thinking if they were that character. Then continue the drama.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage a second time.

The following is an example of the drama and possible responses.

The storyteller introduces the list of guilty men and tells us the four guilty men from the family of Jeshua, son of Jozadak. The men are Levite priests.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing the storyteller, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* These are the men who had foreign wives; or
* I am pleased. The elders worked hard to find the men who were unfaithful; or
* Even the priests and the other Levites were unfaithful and did not follow Yahweh's law.

Ask the person playing the guilty Levite priest descendants of Jeshua: Maaseiah, Eliezer, Jarib, and Gedaliah, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We feel ashamed. We did not know that we were unfaithful to Yahweh; or
* We did not learn Yahweh's laws for us when we were in Babylon; or
* We will learn from Ezra and follow Yahweh's laws from now on.

Continue the drama.

The storyteller tells us that the guilty men promise to separate themselves from their wives and each give a ram as a guilt offering.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing the storyteller, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* These men made the correct offering for their guilt.

Ask the person playing the guilty Levite priest descendants of Jeshua: Maaseiah, Eliezer, Jarib, and Gedaliah, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We are so sorry for our mistake. We do not want Yahweh to be angry with us; or
* We want to follow Yahweh's laws; or
* We have made the right offering to God to pay for our sin; or
* We hope Yahweh will not punish Israel anymore.

Continue the drama.

The storyteller tells us the two guilty men who are descendants of Immer, the five guilty men who are descendants of Harim, and the six guilty men who are descendants of Pashhur. All the men are Levite priests.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing the guilty descendants of Immer, Harim, and Pashhur, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We made a terrible mistake; or
* We want to follow Yahweh's laws and be faithful priests; or
* We feel ashamed.

Continue the drama.

The storyteller tells us six more Levite men who are guilty.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing the guilty Levites: Jozabad, Shimei, Kelaiah, Pethahiah, Judah, and Eliezer, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We want to serve Yahweh and be faithful to Yahweh; or
* We will follow Yahweh's laws from now on; or
* We hope Yahweh will not punish us anymore.

Continue the drama.

The storyteller tells us that one man from the musician Levites is guilty and that three men from the gatekeeper Levites are guilty.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing the guilty musician, Eliashib, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* I made a mistake because I did not know the law; or
* I will do the right thing now and send my wife away; or
* I want to serve Yahweh in the temple, as my ancestors did.

Ask the person playing the guilty gatekeepers, Shallum, Telem, and Uri, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We are very sorry that we had wives who were not Israelites; or
* We will follow Yahweh's laws; or
* We feel sad that our wives are gone, but we must obey our elders.

Filling the Gaps
----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:18–24 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will discuss key terms and words in this passage.

Some of the male **descendants** or "sons" of the **priests** had **married** **foreign** women. You will remember that the storyteller uses the word sons to mean male descendants. Use the same words or phrases for descendants or sons, priests, married, and foreign as you used in previous passages. For more information on descendants and priests, refer to the Master Glossary.

The descendants of Joshua "gave their hands in pledge" to put away their wives. Each man shook or clasped his hand with an elder's hand as a sign of the man's promise to separate from his foreign wife or wives.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for "**gave their hands in pledge**." Pause this audio here.

The men presented a ram to Yahweh as an offering for their **guilt**. Use the same words or phrases for ram and guilt as you used in previous passages. For more information on guilt, refer to the Master Glossary. A ram is an adult male sheep.

Stop here and, if needed, look at a picture of a ram as a group. Pause this audio here.

The men took the rams from the flock, the group of rams that the Israelites kept for offerings to Yahweh. A flock can include both sheep and goats.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **flock**. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

The men made guilt offerings. A person makes a guilt offering to ask Yahweh to forgive their sin when the person broke one of Yahweh's laws.

Stop here and discuss as a group what word or phrase you will use for **guilt offering**. Look up guilt offering in the Master Glossary for more information. If you have already translated this word in another book of the Bible, use the same word that you have used there. Pause this audio here.

The storyteller tells us the guilty men who are **Levites**, **musicians**, and **gatekeepers**. Use the same words or phrases for Levites, musicians, and gatekeepers as you used in previous passages. For more information on Levites, refer to the Master Glossary.

Speaking the Word
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of the passage in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this session, retell the passage, as a group, in your own language.

First, the whole group should practice telling the passage in your own language. Remember to include the things you decided in previous steps, like chronology, words, phrases, emotions, or anything else you discussed.

One group member should tell a few sentences of the passage and pause. Another group member should tell the next part of the passage and pause. Do this until the group has retold the whole passage. The group members can correct each other in this step.

Pause this audio here.

Next, each member of the group should tell the whole passage without interruption at least one time. A group member can use random objects, motions, or their storyboard to help them remember the passage.

Pause this audio here.

Next, the group can decide whose version of the passage you like the most. You may decide that you liked the way one group member told one scene but you liked the way a different group member told another scene.

Pause this audio here.

Finally, the group can put together a final version of the passage that everyone agrees on. Each group member should practice telling this final version of the passage.

* **Associated Passages:** Ezra 10:18-24
* **Associated Articles:** Ram (ID: `a331@FIAImages`); Ram (ID: `a332@FIAImages`); Ram (ID: `a333@FIAImages`); priest (ID: `eng-t103-v1@FIAKeyTerms`); descendant (ID: `eng-t234-v2@FIAKeyTerms`); Levite (ID: `eng-t244-v1@FIAKeyTerms`)

* **Associated ACAI Concepts:** Elijah (ID: `person:Elijah.3`); Judah (ID: `person:Judah.5`); Pethahiah (ID: `person:Pethahiah.2`); Harim (ID: `person:Harim`); Jozabad (ID: `person:Jozabad.7`); Eliezer (ID: `person:Eliezer.10`); Jozabad (ID: `person:Jozabad.8`); Nethanel (ID: `person:Nethanel.8`); Maaseiah (ID: `person:Maaseiah.8`); Elioenai (ID: `person:Elioenai.4`); Eliashib (ID: `person:Eliashib.4`); Shimei (ID: `person:Shimei.15`); Jehiel (ID: `person:Jehiel.9`); Elasah (ID: `person:Elasah`); Uzziah (ID: `person:Uzziah.4`); Maaseiah (ID: `person:Maaseiah.6`); Telem (ID: `person:Telem`); Jozadak (ID: `person:Jozadak.2`); Maaseiah (ID: `person:Maaseiah.7`); Uri (ID: `person:Uri.3`); Kelaiah (ID: `person:Kelaiah`); Hanani (ID: `person:Hanani.3`); Jarib (ID: `person:Jarib.3`); Zebadiah (ID: `person:Zebadiah.9`); Shallum (ID: `person:Shallum.10`); Gedaliah (ID: `person:Gedaliah`); Ishmael (ID: `person:Ishmael.6`); Shemaiah (ID: `person:Shemaiah.16`); Eliezer (ID: `person:Eliezer.9`); Pashhur (ID: `person:Pashhur`); Tribe of Levi (ID: `group:Levi`); Jeshua (ID: `person:Jeshua`); Levi (ID: `person:Levi.3`); Immer (ID: `person:Immer.2`); Sheep (ID: `fauna:Lamb`); Goat (ID: `fauna:Goat`); Flock (ID: `fauna:Flock`)

## Ezra 10:25–44 (id: eng-ezr-p21b-v1)

Hear and Heart
--------------

In this step, hear Ezra 10:25–44 and put it in your hearts.

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:25–44 three times, in three different translations, if possible.

Pause this audio here.

Now, as a group, discuss the following questions:

1. What do you like in this passage? Pause this audio here.
2. What do you not like or not understand in this passage? Pause this audio here.
3. What does this passage tell us about God? Pause this audio here.
4. What does this passage tell us about people? Pause this audio here.
5. How does this passage affect our daily lives? Pause this audio here.
6. Who do you know who needs to hear this passage?

Setting the Stage
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:25–44 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this passage, the storyteller continues to tell us the names of the men who are guilty of having wives who are not Israelites. In the last story, the storyteller told us about the Levites who were guilty. Now, the storyteller tells us about the men from family groups who are not Levites who were guilty. The men are Israelites from the other tribes of Israel. The storyteller lists several family groups with guilty men. Not all of the family groups that returned to Jerusalem with Zerubbabel included guilty men. The storyteller names four family groups that did not return to Jerusalem with Zerubbabel. The men are all descendants of an important ancestor in their family. We do not know when the important ancestor was alive, and the important ancestor is probably dead when this story happens.

The storyteller tells us that seven sons or descendants of Parosh are guilty. The guilty men are Ramiah, Izziah, Malkijah, Mijamin, Eleazar, Malkijah, and Benaiah. There are probably two descendants of Parosh called Malkijah.

Stop here and discuss this question as a group: Talk about people in your family or community who have the same name as each other. How do you know which person someone is talking about? Pause this audio here.

The storyteller tells us that six descendants or sons of Elam are guilty. The guilty men are Mattaniah, Zechariah, Jehiel, Abdi, Jeremoth, and Elijah.

The storyteller tells us that six descendants or sons of Zattu are guilty. The guilty men are Elioenai, Eliashib, Mattaniah, Jeremoth, Zabad, and Aziza.

The storyteller tells us that four descendants or sons of Bebai are guilty. The guilty men are Jehohanan, Hananiah, Zabbai, and Athlai. The storyteller of Nehemiah tells us that Zabbai helped to repair the wall of Jerusalem.

The storyteller tells us that six descendants or sons of Bani are guilty. The guilty men are Meshullam, Malluch, Adaiah, Jashub, Sheal, and Jeremoth. We do not know if Meshullam is the same man as the Meshullam who objected to the leaders' plan when Ezra called all the men to Jerusalem earlier in the book of Ezra.

The storyteller tells us that eight descendants or sons of Pahath\-Moab are guilty. The guilty men are Adna, Kelal, Benaiah, Maaseiah, Mattaniah, Bezalel, Binnui, and Manasseh.

The storyteller tells us that eight descendants or sons of Harim are guilty. The guilty men are Eliezer, Ishijah, Malkijah, Shemaiah, Shimeon, Benjamin, Malluch, and Shemariah. This Malkijah is a different man from the two descendants of Parosh also named Malkijah.

The storyteller tells us that seven descendants or sons of Hashum are guilty. The guilty men are Mattenai, Mattattah, Zabad, Eliphelet, Jeremai, Manasseh, and Shimei. This Manasseh is a different man from the descendant of Pahath\-Moab also named Manasseh.

The storyteller tells us that 12 descendants or sons of Bani are guilty. This is a different family group from the descendants of Bani that the storyteller told us about earlier in the story. It is possible that there were two different men named Bani, and so this was a different family from the one we heard about already. However, it is also possible that the storyteller recorded the name of the men's ancestor incorrectly. The guilty men are Maadai, Amram, Uel, Benaiah, Bedeiah, Keluhi, Vaniah, Meremoth, Eliashib, Mattaniah, Mattenai, and Jaasu. The men are different from the men with the same names in other family groups.

The storyteller tells us that 13 descendants or sons of Binnui are guilty. The guilty men are Shimei, Shelemiah, Nathan, Adaiah, Macnadebai, Shashai, Sharai, Azarel, Shelemiah, Shemariah, Shallum, Amariah, and Joseph.

The storyteller tells us that seven descendants or sons of Nebo are guilty. The guilty men are Jeiel, Mattithiah, Zabad, Zebina, Jaddai, Joel, and Benaiah.

The storyteller finishes the story by telling us that all the men named in the list in this story and the Levites in the previous story took women who were not Israelites into their homes. The women were wives to the Israelite men in the same way that Israelite women were wives to the Israelite men. There are two possible translations of the last part of the story. In some translations, the storyteller tells us that some of the Israelite men had children with the foreign women. In other translations, the storyteller tells us that the Israelite men sent away the foreign women with the Israelite men's children. It seems that the storyteller wants us to know that the Israelite men also sent away the children that the men had with their foreign wives.

Defining the Scenes
-------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:25–44 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will define the scenes, characters, and setting of this passage. Then the group will visualize this passage.

This passage has three scenes.

**In the first scene:** The storyteller tells us about the Israelites who are guilty and who are not Levites.

**In the second scene:** The storyteller tells us the family groups of the guilty men and the names of the guilty men in each family group. Seven descendants of Parosh are guilty. Six descendants of Elam are guilty. Six descendants of Zattu are guilty. Four descendants of Bebai are guilty. Six descendants of Bani are guilty. Eight descendants of Pahath\-Moab are guilty. Eight descendants of Harim are guilty. Seven descendants of Hashum are guilty. Twelve descendants of Bani are guilty. Thirteen descendants of Binnui are guilty. Seven descendants of Nebo are guilty.

**In the third scene:** The storyteller ends the list and tells us that all the men in the list had foreign wives. Some of the Israelite men had children with the foreign women and sent away the children with their mothers.

The characters in this passage are:

* Storyteller
* Guilty men who are descendants of Parosh, Elam, Zattu, Bebai, Bani, Pahath\-Moab, Harim, Hashum, Bani, Binnui, and Nebo
* And the children born to Israelite fathers and foreign women

As a group, pay attention to these parts of the passage's setting:

This passage continues on immediately after the previous passage. In this passage, the storyteller completes the list of Israelite men who are guilty of having foreign wives. In the previous passage, the storyteller listed all the Israelite Levite men who were guilty. Now the storyteller tells us all the other Israelite men who are guilty. The storyteller divides the list into groups of men according to the family that each man belongs to. Each family group is identified as the descendants or sons of an important ancestor. Most scholars say there are 11 family groups with guilty men in the family group. However, some scholars say there are 12 family groups. The first group of men is the descendants of Parosh. The guilty men are Ramiah, Izziah, Malkijah, Mijamin, Eleazar, Malkijah, and Benaiah.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together seven small objects and place them in a group in front of you. The seven objects represent the seven guilty men. Pause this audio here.

The second group of men is the descendants of Elam. The guilty men are Mattaniah, Zechariah, Jehiel, Abdi, Jeremoth, and Elijah.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together six more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The third group of men is the descendants of Zattu. The guilty men are Elioenai, Eliashib, Mattaniah, Jeremoth, Zabad, and Aziza.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together six more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The fourth group of men is the descendants of Bebai. The guilty men are Johanan, Hananiah, Zabbai, and Athlai.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together four more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The fifth group of men is the descendants of Bani. The guilty men are Meshullam, Malluch, Adaiah, Jashub, Sheal, and Jeremoth.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together six more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The sixth group of men is the descendants of Pahath\-Moab. The guilty men are Adna, Kelal, Benaiah, Maaseiah, Mattaniah, Bezalel, Binnui, and Manasseh.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together eight more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The seventh group of men is the descendants of Harim. The guilty men are Eliezer, Ishijah, Malkijah, Shemaiah, Shimeon, Benjamin, Malluch, and Shemariah.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together eight more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The eighth group of men is the descendants of Hashum. The guilty men are Mattenai, Mattattah, Zabad, Eliphelet, Jeremai, Manasseh, and Shimei.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together seven more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The ninth group of men is the descendants of Bani. The guilty men are Maadai, Amram, Uel, Benaiah, Bedeiah, Keluhi, Vaniah, Meremoth, Eliashib, Mattaniah, Mattenai, and Jaasu.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together 12 more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The tenth group of men is the descendants of Binnui. The guilty men are Shimei, Shelemiah, Nathan, Adaiah, Macnadebai, Shashai, Sharai, Azarel, Shelemiah, Shemariah, Shallum, Amariah, and Joseph.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together 13 more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Pause this audio here.

The last group of men is the descendants of Nebo. The guilty men are Jeiel, Matthithiah, Zabad, Zebina, Jaddai, Joel, and Benaiah.

Stop here and do this activity as a group: Collect together seven more small objects and place them together in a group next to, but separate from, your objects from the activity before this one. Notice all the different objects, which represent all the guilty Israelite men who are not Levite men. Pause this audio here.

The storyteller ends the story with a reminder to us that all the men in the list, Levites and other Israelites, married foreign women. The storyteller gives us a final piece of information that some of the Israelite men had children with their foreign wives. The Israelite men also sent away their own children with the children's mothers.

Now, the group should storyboard, draw, or use objects to visualize the passage and the action in it.

Embodying the Text
------------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:25–44 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will dramatize the passage.

This passage has three scenes.

The characters in this passage are:

* Storyteller
* Guilty men who are descendants of Parosh, Elam, Zattu, Bebai, Bani, Pahath\-Moab, Harim, Hashum, Bani, Binnui, and Nebo
* And the children born to Israelite fathers and foreign women

As a group, act out the passage twice. You should act out the passage in your own language.

First, act out the passage without stopping. Pay attention to the dialogue, flow, plotline, and chronology of the passage. Make sure you do not skip acting out the difficult or important parts of the passage. Help each other remember every part of the passage.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage.

The group should act out this passage a second time. At certain points in the drama, pause the drama and ask the person playing the character, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person playing the character should answer what they would be feeling or thinking if they were that character. Then continue the drama.

Pause this audio here and act out the passage a second time.

The following is an example of the drama and possible responses.

The storyteller tells us about the Israelites who are guilty and who are not Levites.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing the storyteller, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Look, not all of the guilty men were Levites. There were also men from the other tribes of Israel; or
* Many men did not know Yahweh's laws; or
* Many men sent away their foreign wives.

Continue the drama.

The storyteller tells us the family groups of the guilty men and the names of the guilty men in each family group. Seven descendants of Parosh are guilty. Six descendants of Elam are guilty. Six descendants of Zattu are guilty. Four descendants of Bebai are guilty. Six descendants of Bani are guilty. Eight descendants of Pahath\-Moab are guilty. Eight descendants of Harim are guilty. Seven descendants of Hashum are guilty. Twelve descendants of Bani are guilty. Thirteen descendants of Binnui are guilty. Seven descendants of Nebo are guilty.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing the guilty men who are descendants of Parosh, Elam, Zattu, Bebai, Bani, Pahath\-Moab, Harim, Hashum, Bani, Binnui, and Nebo, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* We feel so ashamed. We did not know Yahweh's laws; or
* The Levites are supposed to help us obey Yahweh. But when we saw that some of the Levites took foreign wives, we decided to do it too; or
* We will miss our wives, but we promised Ezra and our elders to send our foreign wives away; or
* Will Yahweh still be angry with us? Did we do everything to stop Yahweh's anger? or
* Now we will follow Yahweh's laws and only have Israelite wives.

Continue the drama.

The storyteller ends the list and tells us that all the men in the list had foreign wives. Some of the Israelite men had children with the foreign women and sent away the children with those children's mothers.

Pause the drama. Ask the person playing the storyteller, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* There were lots of men who married foreign women in the same way that an Israelite man marries an Israelite woman; or
* The guilty men kept their promises to Ezra and the Israelite elders; or
* It was a terrible time. The Israelite men sent away not only their foreign wives, but also the children they had with those wives.

Ask the person playing the children born to Israelite fathers and foreign women, "What are you feeling or thinking?" The person might answer things like:

* Why do we have to leave our homes? or
* We are sad to leave our fathers and our homes; or
* Where will we go and who will look after us and our mothers?

Filling the Gaps
----------------

Listen to an audio version of Ezra 10:25–44 in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this step, the group will discuss key terms and words in this passage.

The storyteller tells us the guilty men who are from the rest of the **Israelites**, the Israelites who are not Levites. Use the same word or phrase for Israelites as you used in previous passages. For more information on Israelites, refer to the Master Glossary.

The storyteller tells us the guilty men who are the **descendants** or **sons** of different significant ancestors. Use the same words or phrases for descendants or sons as you used in previous passages where sons meant descendants. For more information on descendants, refer to the Master Glossary.

All the men in the list **married** **foreign** women. Use the same words or phrases for married and foreign as you used in previous passages.

Some of the men had children with the foreign women or "**wives**." Use the same word or phrase for wives as you used in previous passages.

Speaking the Word
-----------------

Listen to an audio version of the passage in the easiest\-to\-understand translation.

Pause this audio here.

In this session, retell the passage, as a group, in your own language.

First, the whole group should practice telling the passage in your own language. Remember to include the things you decided in previous steps, like chronology, words, phrases, emotions, or anything else you discussed.

One group member should tell a few sentences of the passage and pause. Another group member should tell the next part of the passage and pause. Do this until the group has retold the whole passage. The group members can correct each other in this step.

Pause this audio here.

Next, each member of the group should tell the whole passage without interruption at least one time. A group member can use random objects, motions, or their storyboard to help them remember the passage.

Pause this audio here.

Next, the group can decide whose version of the passage you like the most. You may decide that you liked the way one group member told one scene but you liked the way a different group member told another scene.

Pause this audio here.

Finally, the group can put together a final version of the passage that everyone agrees on. Each group member should practice telling this final version of the passage.
